<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T5 findings for Conscience cleansed through atonement received -->

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence shows transformation operating on both condition and orientation, though with differing emphases across VCGs. Condition change is the primary emphasis: throughout VCG-01, the explicit outcome formulas ("he shall be forgiven," Lev 4:20, 4:26, 4:31, etc.) describe an objective change in the person's standing before God — guilt is objectively removed, not merely perceived differently. Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) describes sins remembered "no more" — an objective change in divine disposition toward the person. Rom 3:25 (VCG-05) describes former sins being "passed over" — objective condition change. Orientation change also appears: Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) is the most direct evidence — the atoned person is not merely pardoned but moved to "wordless shame and humiliation" as an inner-being response to being covered. Pro 16:6 (VCG-04) links atonement and the fear of the Lord with "turning from evil" — moral reorientation accompanies the covering. Isa 27:9 (VCG-07) shows atonement as tied to the removal of idolatrous orientation — the turn from idolatry is both condition of and result of atonement. Dan 9:24 (VCG-07) frames atonement in the context of "bringing in everlasting righteousness" — suggesting a comprehensive transformation rather than only pardon. The corpus predominantly emphasizes objective condition change (guilt removed, forgiven) but consistently implies that genuine reception produces orientation transformation as well.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence shows two distinguishable mechanism-contexts. (1) Ritual-priestly mechanism (OT): In VCG-01 and VCG-02, change is produced through the priest-mediated sacrifice — the mechanism requires a specified animal, prescribed action, and priestly enactment. The human posture required is bringing the offering (faith expressed ritually). The mechanism is external, priestly, and repeatable — each new sin requires a new atoning act. The change is instantaneous at the point of the priest's completing the ritual. (2) Faith-propitiation mechanism (NT): In VCG-05, the mechanism is entirely Christ-centred and received through faith rather than through repeated ritual. Rom 3:25 specifies faith in his blood as the access mode. Heb 2:17 emphasizes sympathetic solidarity as enabling the effective propitiation. 1Jo 2:2 presents Christ as a standing provision ("he is the propitiation") — once-for-all rather than requiring re-enactment. The mechanism-difference between OT and NT is: OT = prescribed sacrifice + priestly mediation + repeated; NT = Christ's blood + faith-reception + once-for-all. VCG-04's divine-initiative cases (Psa 65:3, Psa 78:38, Isa 6:7) represent a third mechanism-type: direct divine-compassion atonement outside the standard sacrificial system, suggesting God is not mechanistically bound to the ritual system even while providing it. The evidence thus distinguishes three mechanism-contexts, each operating in its own contextual mode.
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent on formation and sanctification, though the connection is partial. Pro 16:6, Isa 27:9, and Eze 16:63 provide the primary formation-relevant evidence. See T5.5.1 and T5.5.2 above. This prompt requires no silence notation, though the formation dimension is subsidiary rather than primary in this characteristic's corpus.
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence presents a mixed picture with variation across contexts. Evidence for irreversibility: Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) states sins will be "remembered no more" — the New Covenant promise implies a permanent removal of remembered guilt. Dan 9:24 (VCG-07) frames atonement as an eschatological, once-for-all act producing "everlasting righteousness" — the permanence marker ("everlasting") implies irreversibility. 1Jo 2:2 frames Christ's hilasmos as a standing provision rather than a repeated act. Evidence for conditional/reversible transformation within the OT system: VCG-01's repeated atonement formulas (Lev 4–6) imply that each new sin requires new atonement — the transformed state does not prevent future guilt-accumulation. The persistent-sin cases in VCG-06 show that ongoing unrepentance can close the atonement pathway (1Sa 3:14) — suggesting that the transformed state requires sustained relational alignment to remain available. Psa 78:38 (VCG-04) notes God "atoning repeatedly" for Israel's recurrent sin — suggesting the OT atonement was regularly renewed rather than once-for-all. The evidence distinguishes between the OT sacrificial system (requiring repeated atonement, transformation potentially disrupted by new sin) and the NT once-for-all propitiation (Heb 8:12, 1Jo 2:2) where transformation is presented as more permanently secured. The irreversibility question resolves differently under each system.
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent on mechanism; substitutionary sacrifice, priestly mediation, faith-reception, and direct divine action are all documented as mechanisms across VCGs. See T5.3.1 and T5.3.2. This prompt requires no silence notation.
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence contains explicit eschatological orientation. Dan 9:24 (VCG-07) is the most direct: the seventy-weeks decree includes "to atone for iniquity" as one of six goals, alongside "to put an end to sin," "to bring in everlasting righteousness," "to seal both vision and prophet," and "to anoint a most holy place" — atonement is named as part of a comprehensive eschatological program. The "everlasting righteousness" that accompanies this atonement marks its orientation as permanent and final rather than provisional. Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) presents the New Covenant's "remember sins no more" as the fulfillment of God's promise — the eschatological new covenant reality surpasses the OT provisional covering. 1Jo 2:2 (VCG-05) and Rom 3:25 (VCG-05) present Christ's propitiation as a once-for-all event that addresses "former sins passed over" and provides universal coverage — the once-for-all nature implies an eschatological sufficiency. 1Jo 4:10 (VCG-04) frames the sending of the Son as the culminating act of divine love, implying a decisive, unrepeatable moment. The trajectory in the corpus moves from repeated provisional OT atonement (VCG-01) through prophetic eschatological promise (Dan 9:24) to the once-for-all Christ-event (VCG-05) and the New Covenant's permanent forgiveness (Heb 8:12). The present operation of atonement is oriented toward the fullness in which sin is finally and permanently covered and righteousness is everlastingly established.
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent on transformation; it is extensively documented in both objective (condition) and subjective (orientation) registers. See T5.1.1 and T5.1.2 above. This prompt requires no silence notation.
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence shows limited but meaningful connection between atonement and suffering/affliction. The clearest instance is Psa 78:38 (VCG-04): Israel's suffering under divine wrath is the context in which God's atoning compassion operates — God repeatedly atones and averts further destruction, so affliction (ongoing judgment under sin's weight) is the context from which atonement rescues. Psa 79:9 (VCG-04) arises from a context of national catastrophe ("help us, O God of our salvation, deliver us"): the plea for atonement is embedded in a prayer of distress — affliction prompts the cry for covering. Luk 18:13 (VCG-05) presents the tax collector's posture of inner suffering — crushed, self-condemned, unable to approach — as the context and posture that makes atonement-seeking genuine. Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) shows post-atonement shame as a form of inner suffering — the memory of covered sin produces ongoing contrition. The broader corpus does not present physical affliction as a mechanism that produces atonement or as a result of atonement. Rather, the relationship is: moral guilt-weight (a form of inner suffering) is the condition in which atonement operates; received atonement relieves that inner suffering; ongoing memory of the guilt (Eze 16:63) produces a chastened, shame-bearing state. Suffering is the context and fuel for atonement-seeking rather than a mechanism for producing atonement.
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The present experience of atonement in the evidence anticipates several dimensions of its future fullness. (1) From repeated to once-for-all: The OT sacrificial cycle (VCG-01's repeated sin-offering-forgiveness pattern, Psa 78:38's "repeatedly") anticipates a final atoning act that eliminates the need for repetition — the once-for-all propitiation of Rom 3:25 and 1Jo 2:2. Present partial atonement anticipates complete and permanent covering. (2) From covered-but-remembered to never-remembered-again: The OT conscience-cleansed state still carries forward the memory of sins (Eze 16:63 shows shame at remembered sins even after atonement) — the New Covenant promise of Heb 8:12 ("I will remember their sins no more") anticipates a future state in which guilt is not merely covered but wholly removed from divine memory. (3) From provisional to everlasting: Dan 9:24's "everlasting righteousness" as the eschatological companion to completed atonement anticipates a future state where the cleared conscience produces permanent moral standing rather than provisional right-standing. (4) From partial scope to universal: The OT's bounded covenant scope (VCG-01, Exo 29:33) anticipates 1Jo 2:2's "whole world" — the future fullness encompasses all who receive it. Present atonement-experience is a foretaste and partial instance of the permanent, universal, once-for-all conscience-cleansed state that the eschatological fulfillment secures.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence describes a consistent three-stage sequence across multiple VCGs, most clearly in VCG-01 and VCG-05. Before: The person is in a state of accumulated, recognized, or overwhelming guilt — "sin-laden" (Lev 5:6, "guilt surfacing"), "overwhelmed by iniquities" (Psa 65:3), "conscience struck" (Luk 18:13, beating the breast), "standing at distance" (Luk 18:13). The before-state involves guilt that is real and subjectively felt. During: The atonement act itself — the priest mediates, the blood is offered, the hand is laid (Lev 1:4), the coal touches the lips (Isa 6:7), Christ is set forth as hilastērios (Rom 3:25). This transitional moment involves a mechanism that effects the covering. After: The person is "forgiven" (Lev 4:20 and throughout VCG-01), guilt "removed" (Isa 6:7), sins "remembered no more" (Heb 8:12), "justified" (implied in Luk 18:14, contextually following the tax collector's prayer), standing in "right-standing before God" restored. Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) adds a further after-state: shame and silenced contrition as the response to being atoned-for — guilt remembered but covered, producing humility rather than ongoing condemnation. The sequence is: guilt-burdened → atoning act received → conscience-cleansed with secondary humility.
- *T5.4.2* — _Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence shows that suffering functions primarily to reveal and deepen the atonement-seeking posture rather than to produce atonement itself. Psa 65:3 ("when iniquities overwhelm me") shows that the experience of being overwhelmed — a form of inner affliction — reveals the person's utter dependence on God's covering, driving them toward God rather than away. Psa 78:38 shows Israel's repeated experience of near-destruction functioning (despite the people's stubbornness) as the repeated occasion for God's atoning compassion — suffering under divine wrath is the context in which atonement's necessity becomes undeniable. Luk 18:13's tax collector is in a state of inner anguish that produces the archetypal atonement-seeking posture — the suffering of condemned conscience drives him to the only available recourse. Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) shows that post-atonement shame (a form of inner suffering) deepens the person's awareness of what they were covered from — suffering functions to sustain humility and gratitude in the atoned person. The evidence does not show physical suffering producing atonement or being required for it. Rather: inner suffering (conscience-weight, overwhelming guilt) reveals the need; affliction in the context of divine judgment reveals its source; post-atonement shame sustains the characterological impact of having been covered.
- *T5.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent on eschatological trajectory; Dan 9:24, Heb 8:12, and the once-for-all propitiation cluster (VCG-05) all address it. See T5.6.1 and T5.6.2 above. This prompt requires no silence notation.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The sequence reveals that atonement works through objective substitution received by the person in a posture of acknowledged need, producing an inner-being shift that is both declarative (guilt removed by divine pronouncement) and experiential (felt as relief, peace, and secondary shame). State 1 — Guilt-burdened: The person is under the weight of real, recognized sin. The texts name this as "sin-laden" (VCG-01 keywords), "overwhelmed" (Psa 65:3), self-condemned and distanced (Luk 18:13). The guilt is both objective (actual transgression before God) and subjective (inner-being weight). State 2 — Approach/presentation: The person brings the offering, lays hands (Lev 1:4), pays the ransom (Exo 30:15–16), prays (Luk 18:13), or trusts Christ (Rom 3:25). The transition requires an active posture — faith, contrition, or prescribed ritual action. State 3 — Forgiven/accepted: The outer declaration ("he shall be forgiven") and inner shift (guilt objectively removed) occur simultaneously. The conscience is cleared by an external act ratified by God. State 4 (secondary, not always present) — Shame/contrition/moral turning: Eze 16:63 and Pro 16:6 and Isa 27:9 document a post-atonement inner state of humbled awareness, moral reorientation, and fear of God. The sequence reveals that this characteristic works through externally mediated, divinely ratified objective removal of guilt — inner transformation follows the objective change rather than preceding it.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not entirely silent on the suffering relationship; several verses address it in the modes described in T5.4.1 and T5.4.2 above. However, the connection is partial and indirect — suffering as a category is not systematically treated in this evidence block. The evidence does not address physical suffering as a mechanism of atonement, and the relationship remains largely implied rather than explicitly developed.
- *T5.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is o…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent on sequence; it is explicitly documented in the before/during/after logic of VCG-01's outcome formulas and in VCG-05's reception-through-faith pattern. See T5.2.1 and T5.2.2 above. This prompt requires no silence notation.
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence shows limited but genuine connection to the formation arc, concentrated in particular verses. Pro 16:6 (VCG-04) explicitly joins atonement to long-term moral transformation: "by steadfast love and faithfulness iniquity is atoned for, and by the fear of the Lord one turns away from evil" — the atoning function produces and is joined to the moral turning that characterizes sanctification. Isa 27:9 (VCG-07) presents atonement as tied to the elimination of idolatrous patterns: "this will be the full fruit of the removal of his sin" — atonement is not merely pardon but the result of genuine cultic and moral purification. Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) shows the atoned person being permanently marked by shame and humility — the memory of being covered reshapes the person's posture over time, functioning as a formative force. Psa 78:38 (VCG-04) shows the formation arc in negative relief: God's repeated atoning mercies toward persistently sinful Israel are part of the long historical pedagogy that shapes the people's understanding of divine compassion and their own need. The NT passages do not directly address sanctification in this evidence block, though Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) implies that forgiven-and-remembered-no-more establishes the foundation for new covenant moral formation. The evidence addresses formation tangentially rather than as a central theme.
- *T5.6.3* — _If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence contains limited but notable generational-scope evidence. Deu 21:8 (VCG-07) shows corporate blood-guilt resolved through priestly intercession that covers the community rather than just an individual — the atoning act has communal and generational scope (the land is cleared of inherited blood-guilt). Exo 30:15–16 (VCG-03) establishes atonement-coverage as a structural feature of Israel's national identity across generations — the ransom payment is a generational institution. Psa 78:38 (VCG-04) shows God's atoning mercy operating across generations of Israel's repeated failure — the deposit of God's compassionate atoning character is carried forward through Israel's generational experience of being repeatedly covered. However, the evidence does not directly address individual atonement producing deposits that transfer generationally to descendants. VCG-06's 1Sa 3:14 suggests that persistent priestly sin's consequences can extend across the family ("the iniquity of Eli's house"), which by symmetry implies that atoned standing may also have household or generational implications — but this is an inference from the negative case rather than direct positive evidence. The generational-consequence dimension is partially evidenced at the corporate/national level but is largely silent at the individual-generational level.
- *T5.7.1* — _Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The primary mechanism across the corpus is substitutionary sacrifice received through mediatorial act, producing declarative/sudden objective change rather than gradual formation. VCG-02 makes the mechanism explicit: Lev 17:11 names blood-on-the-altar as the mechanism — "the life of the flesh is in the blood, and I have given it for you on the altar to make atonement for your souls." Lev 1:4 shows the mechanism as substitution activated by identification: hand-laying transfers the offerer's identity to the animal, which is then accepted in their place. VCG-01's repeated "he shall be forgiven" formulas describe an instantaneous declarative outcome — the change occurs at the moment the atoning act is completed. Isa 6:7 presents the mechanism as a direct divine-touch through an angelic agent — instantaneous and transformative in the moment. Rom 3:25 (VCG-05) frames the mechanism as Christ's blood received through faith — an encounter (with the propitiation) that produces immediate standing-change. The change mechanism is therefore encounter-with-substitutionary-mediation rather than discipline or gradual formation. However, VCG-04's Psa 78:38 shows repeated atonement events suggesting a formative dimension across time within the OT system — the recurring pattern of sin, atonement, and mercy functions to teach Israel the nature of God's compassion. The secondary mechanism of moral transformation (Pro 16:6, Isa 27:9, Eze 16:63) follows the declarative change rather than preceding it, operating through shame and fear of God post-atonement.
- *T5.7.2* — _Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence reveals that atonement functions as the foundational clearing-event that enables the longer formation arc rather than being itself the formative process. The pattern is: sin accumulates, atonement clears the foundation, moral reorientation and fear of God follow. Pro 16:6 (VCG-04) presents this most directly — atonement is not the goal but the clearing that accompanies and enables the moral turn from evil. Isa 27:9 (VCG-07) shows that genuine atonement is evidenced by the demolition of the idolatrous structures — the formation arc (removal of competing loyalties) and the atoning act are interdependent. Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) suggests that the memory of atonement received becomes a formative force in itself — "never open your mouth again because of your shame" describes a permanent characterological reshaping produced by the awareness of having been covered in one's worst state. The role of atonement in the formation arc is therefore: (1) foundational clearing that removes guilt-weight blocking further growth, (2) a revelation of divine character (compassion, mercy, prior love) that reshapes the person's understanding of and orientation toward God, and (3) a post-reception shame and humility that sustains the formation process. Atonement is less a sanctifying discipline and more the necessary precondition and recurring resource for the sanctification process.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Conscience cleansed through atonement received -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The characteristic is named "Conscience cleansed through atonement received." The name is structurally composite and signals several things about its essential nature. First, the primary inner-being locus is the conscience — not the intellect, will, or emotion as such, but the moral-relational faculty that registers guilt and standing before God. Second, the operative verb is "cleansed" — a passive transformation verb, indicating that the conscience does not cleanse itself but is cleansed by an act done to or for it. Third, "through atonement" names the mechanism — the characteristic is not simply forgiveness-as-abstract-declaration but is specifically mediated through the atonement structure (sacrifice, substitution, propitiation). Fourth, "received" confirms the directional asymmetry: the person is recipient, not agent, of the atonement. The name therefore signals at the definitional level: this is a passively-received, mechanism-mediated, conscience-located transformation from guilt-laden to cleared — and it is structurally dependent on an external atoning act.
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The primary Hebrew term is H3722B ka.phar (the atoned-state use), and the primary Greek terms are G2433 hilaskomai (verb), G2434 hilasmos (noun), G2435 hilastērios (noun), and G2436 hileōs (adjective). At the definitional level, before deeper lexical work:

- **Ka.phar** carries the basic sense of covering — something placed over guilt so that it is no longer exposed to divine view or wrath. The inner-being state named is one of covered-ness: the person is no longer naked before judgment.
- **Hilaskomai** is to propitiate or make propitious — to effect a change in the standing between a holy party and a guilty party, removing the obstacle (guilt/wrath). The inner-being register is relational-positional: the person's standing has shifted.
- **Hilasmos** names the propitiation as a thing — the sin-covering provision that produces the changed standing. Christ himself is the hilasmos (1Jo 2:2; 1Jo 4:10).
- **Hilastērios** names the place or person as the mercy-seat/propitiation-locus — Christ set forth as the place where wrath meets blood and is satisfied (Rom 3:25).
- **Hileōs** is the adjectival state — God being propitious/merciful, favorably disposed toward rather than opposed (Heb 8:12).

Together these terms define the characteristic as: covered, propitiated, standing in a divinely-shifted relational position — guilt hidden, wrath averted, God favorably disposed. The definitional core is relational-positional covering.
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, all three types of implication are present in the name "Conscience cleansed through atonement received":

**Directional**: "Received" establishes the directionality immediately — the characteristic moves from outside the person inward, from divine-or-priestly act toward the human conscience. This is not a self-generated state; the enquiry is oriented from the outset toward the question of source and mechanism rather than personal cultivation or development.

**Relational**: "Conscience" is inherently a relational faculty — it registers standing in relation to a moral authority (ultimately God). "Atonement" is structurally relational — it presupposes a ruptured relationship between guilty party and holy party, and its function is relational repair. The name orients the enquiry toward the God-human relational axis as the primary register.

**Constitutional**: "Conscience cleansed" locates the characteristic constitutionally in the deep moral-inner faculty of the person, not in behavior, external status alone, or emotion. The name signals that the transformation occurs at the level of the person's inner moral self-awareness, not merely their legal standing in an abstract register. This orients the enquiry toward the inner-being constitutional question of what kind of inner faculty is engaged and transformed.

Together, the name establishes from the outset: this is a divinely-directed (inward from outside), relational (God-person repair), constitutionally-located (conscience) phenomenon.
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The characteristic appears primarily to be a condition — a state of inner being produced by an external act and persisting as the person's standing before God. The Levitical atonement outcomes (M38-D-VCG-01: "forgiven," "guilt removed," "conscience cleansed") describe a resultant state following the priestly act, not an ongoing disposition or a single moment of action by the person. Rom 3:25 (M38-D-VCG-05) presents propitiation as something received through faith, establishing a lasting condition of wrath-averted standing. Heb 8:12 (M38-D-VCG-04) frames sins remembered no more as a permanent condition-shift. However, Luk 18:13 (M38-D-VCG-05) shows that the inner-being posture of receiving atonement includes an act of confession and self-presentation ("be merciful to me"), and Eze 16:63 (M38-D-VCG-07) shows that the condition once received produces ongoing shame and contrition — suggesting secondary dispositional and actional dimensions. The working answer is: the characteristic is primarily a received condition (cleared standing before God), with constitutive actional prerequisites (contrition, faith, self-presentation) and secondary dispositional effects (ongoing shame, gratitude, moral turning).
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The characteristic is composite rather than simple at first encounter. Even the name itself ("conscience cleansed through atonement received") contains three distinguishable constituent elements: (a) the conscience as the inner-being site, (b) the cleansing as the inner-being transformation, and (c) the atonement received as the external mechanism producing the transformation. The verse evidence confirms this multi-element structure. The Levitical VCG-01 cluster shows a three-part sequence: sin presented → atonement made by priest → forgiveness granted to the offerer. The substitutionary VCG-02 adds a fourth element: identification (hand-laying) as the inner act bridging offerer and offering. The NT VCG-05 propitiation cluster adds faith as a constituent element (Rom 3:25: "through faith"). The characteristic is therefore structurally composite: it involves (1) a sin-burdened inner state, (2) an external atoning act, (3) an inner act of reception (faith, contrition, identification), and (4) the resulting inner state of cleared conscience. These are not alternative descriptions but constituent phases of a single phenomenon.
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Working description: **Conscience cleansed through atonement received is a passively-received, mechanism-mediated moral-relational condition in which the inner person's guilt-bearing conscience is transformed from sin-laden and wrath-facing to covered, cleared, and standing-restored before God — produced by an external atoning act (priestly sacrifice, divine initiative, or christological propitiation) received through faith, contrition, and self-presentation, and carrying both immediate relief from guilt-burden and sustained effects including moral reorientation, humble contrition, eschatological righteousness, and capacity for vocation.**

Constitutional location: the moral-relational conscience — the faculty that registers standing before God in terms of guilt, right-standing, and wrath-exposure.

Faculties primarily engaged: conscience as primary site; will engaged in self-presentation and moral turning (Lev 1:4, Pro 16:6); faith as the receiving-orientation (Rom 3:25); emotional capacity engaged in shame and gratitude (Eze 16:63).

Impact on the person: positional (standing before God changed), moral (will reoriented away from evil), relational (access to God restored and sustained), and eschatological (oriented toward everlasting righteousness).
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — M38-D-VCG-06 (atonement withheld, unavailable, or permanently refused) names the structural opposite directly: the inner-being state of permanent, unresolved guilt with wrath un-averted and conscience uncleaned. 1Sa 3:14 gives the starkest articulation — "the iniquity of Eli's house shall not be atoned for by sacrifice or offering ever" — a condition of closed-off guilt that no sacrificial mechanism can reach. Isa 22:14 and Isa 47:11 describe the state of being helpless before judgment with no atonement available. Num 35:33 (VCG-06) identifies blood-guilt from murder as categorically beyond standard atonement — the inner being faces judgment without covering. Jer 18:23 (VCG-06) shows the prophet invoking this opposite state as a curse on enemies. The structural opposite is therefore: conscience burdened and guilt-permanent, wrath-facing without relief, standing before God condemned rather than cleared. The programme cross-register with M02 Anger (wrath-averted as structural opposite at the God-ward pole) confirms this: where atonement received averts wrath and clears conscience, its opposite is wrath-retained and conscience-condemned.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The characteristic explicitly excludes and resists:

1. **Self-generated moral improvement as a substitute for atonement**: The Levitical corpus makes clear that specific sacrificial acts are required — personal effort, good intentions, or moral reform alone do not produce the inner state of guilt-removed. Isa 22:14 and 1Sa 3:14 (M38-D-VCG-06) show that even religious activity (sacrifice and offering) is insufficient where the atonement-pathway is closed — much less unaided moral effort.

2. **Persistent self-accusation after atonement received**: Heb 8:12's promise that sins will be "remembered no more" structurally resists ongoing self-condemnation in the person who has genuinely received atonement — the conscience-cleared state excludes continued guilt-bearing for covered sin.

3. **Pride and self-sufficiency in approach**: Luk 18:13 (M38-D-VCG-05) implicitly excludes the Pharisaic self-justifying posture (the immediate narrative foil) — the characteristic resists approaching the atonement-mechanism from a position of self-righteousness.

4. **Defiance and hardened indifference**: Isa 47:11 (M38-D-VCG-06) implies that the defiant city's proud self-reliance is precisely what puts atonement out of reach — the characteristic resists the inner posture of "I have no need of covering."

5. **Ritual compliance without sincere heart-seeking**: 2Ch 30:18's positive case (God covers sincere but ritually irregular seekers) implies the exclusion of its negative: ritual compliance without sincere heart-orientation does not guarantee genuine reception.
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The verse evidence permits the following boundary demarcations:

1. **Not mere emotional peace or psychological relief**: The characteristic is a conscience-cleared standing before God, not a subjective feeling of peace. No verse in the corpus describes the inner state in terms of emotional comfort alone — "forgiven" (Lev 4:20 etc.) is a moral-relational declaration, not an emotional description. Where emotion appears (shame in Eze 16:63, contrition in Luk 18:13), it is secondary to and shaped by the conscience-cleared state.

2. **Not self-generated moral improvement**: The entire structure of the characteristic — "received," "through atonement" — excludes the idea that the person produces their own clear standing by becoming morally better. This distinguishes it from repentance (M38's adjacent characteristics) and sanctification.

3. **Not identical to forgiveness as a cognitive knowledge alone**: The characteristic involves conscience transformation, not merely intellectual awareness that one is forgiven. Eze 16:63's shame-response and Luk 18:13's bodily-posture of distance both indicate that genuine reception operates at a deeper level than cognitive assent.

4. **Not permanent liturgical access per se**: The characteristic grants inner-being cleared standing, not automatically all the privileges of holy-place access — Exo 29:33 (VCG-02) shows ordination is required for priestly holy-space activity; atonement is its precondition, not its equivalent.

5. **Not propitiation of an offended human party**: All atonement in this corpus is directed God-ward — even 2Sa 21:3 (VCG-03, David and the Gibeonites) ultimately aims at restoring divine blessing to the land. The characteristic ends at the God-human axis; horizontal human reconciliation is an adjacent but distinct characteristic.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The verse evidence supports at least five distinct modes of operation within the inner person:

1. **Forensic-declarative mode** (M38-D-VCG-01): The priest declares forgiveness as the direct outcome of sacrifice — guilt is objectively removed, and the inner person receives a declared standing-change. Lev 4:20, 4:26, 5:18 all follow the pattern: act → pronouncement → inner state altered.

2. **Substitutionary-identification mode** (M38-D-VCG-02): Through hand-laying (Lev 1:4), the person's inner being is linked to the sacrifice — the covering comes not through declaration alone but through personal identification with the substituted life. The conscience is cleared because another life has been accepted in the person's place.

3. **Ransom-sustaining mode** (M38-D-VCG-03): Atonement operates as ongoing relational coverage — keeping the person "remembered" before God (Exo 30:16), sustaining the person in divine awareness and protection rather than resolving a discrete sin-event.

4. **Gift-reception mode** (M38-D-VCG-04): God himself is the agent — the inner person receives atonement as pure gift, without initiating or completing the mechanism (Psa 65:3, Psa 78:38, 1Jo 4:10). The conscience is cleared by divine action alone.

5. **Transformative-shame mode** (M38-D-VCG-07): Eze 16:63 uniquely shows that received atonement operates not only to clear but to humble and silence — the inner person is left in wordless contrition, shame, and remembered guilt coexisting with forgiveness. This is a secondary mode where the clearing itself becomes a transformative moral event.
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, the corpus evidence supports context- and level-dependent variation in operation:

**By context (individual vs. corporate)**: M38-D-VCG-01 operates primarily at the level of individual sin-event resolution (Lev 4:20–6:7 — named individuals, specific offences, personal forgiveness). M38-D-VCG-03 operates at corporate and communal levels: Exo 30:15–16 covers all Israel through the ransom-levy; Deu 21:8 (VCG-07) addresses community blood-guilt through intercession; 2Ch 30:18 covers an entire worshipping assembly through royal intercession.

**By direction (human-initiated vs. divine-initiated)**: In M38-D-VCG-01 and VCG-02, the mechanism is human-initiated — the offerer brings the sacrifice, the priest performs the act. In M38-D-VCG-04, the direction reverses — God acts first as the agent of atonement (Psa 65:3, Psa 78:38, 1Jo 4:10), and the human person is purely receptive.

**By constitutional level (immediate vs. eschatological)**: The Levitical instances (VCG-01) operate at the level of immediate, event-specific guilt resolution. Dan 9:24 and Heb 8:12 (VCG-07, VCG-04) operate at the eschatological-constitutional level — atonement that reshapes the entire moral status of the person permanently, not addressing a discrete sin but the person's whole standing before God.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, a communicative mode is evidenced, though it is not primary. Two distinct speech-based operations appear:

1. **Priestly declaration as constitutive speech-act** (M38-D-VCG-01): The priest's pronouncement of forgiveness ("he shall be forgiven," repeated across Lev 4:20, 4:26, 5:10, 5:13, 5:18, 6:7) is a performative speech act — not describing a pre-existing state but constituting the forgiven state through authorized declaration. The inner person's conscience is cleared partly through the priest's verbal pronouncement. This is communicative operation in the declarative-pronouncement mode.

2. **Prayer-as-atonement-seeking** (M38-D-VCG-03, VCG-07): 2Ch 30:18 shows Hezekiah praying for God to atone for the people — speech as the vehicle of corporate atonement-seeking. Deu 21:8 involves a formal verbal plea ("accept atonement, O LORD, for your people Israel"). Psa 79:9 is a communal speech-act requesting atonement alongside deliverance. In these cases, speech mediates the reception of atonement by naming the need before God.

3. **Inverse-communicative mode** (VCG-06): Jer 18:23 uses the prophetic speech-act to invoke atonement's absence — prayer can also call for guilt not to be covered. This is communicative operation in the curse/withholding mode.

The characteristic does not have a mode where the person simply speaks themselves into a cleansed state — speech is the vehicle of priestly declaration or prayer, not the source of atonement itself.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The verse evidence yields a varied but dominant pattern. The most frequent immediate inner-being response is relief from sin-burden — the Levitical atonement cluster (M38-D-VCG-01) consistently shows the outcome as "forgiven," with no further elaboration of an emotional register beyond the resolved-guilt state. However, several verses particularize the immediate response more specifically:

- **Eze 16:63** (M38-D-VCG-07): the immediate response is shame and silenced contrition — "so that you may remember and be confounded, and never open your mouth again because of your shame, when I atone for you." The first inner movement is not celebration but wordless humility.
- **Luk 18:13** (M38-D-VCG-05): immediately prior to receiving atonement, the inner posture is crushed sin-awareness and distance — the tax collector stands far off, will not lift his eyes; the immediate response to the propitiatory encounter is dependence rather than confidence.
- **Isa 6:7** (M38-D-VCG-04): the immediate response to lips being atoned is readiness for service — "your guilt is taken away, and your sin atoned for" → immediately followed by "here am I, send me."

The most consistent immediate inner-being response across the full corpus is transition from burdened to relieved — guilt-laden to forgiven — but the texture of that relief ranges from shame-mixed-with-gratitude (Eze 16:63) to readiness-for-action (Isa 6:7) to dependent-contrite-expectation (Luk 18:13).
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The immediate response varies meaningfully across the verse evidence. The dominant response across M38-D-VCG-01 is the declared state of "forgiven" — a positional change registered without elaboration of inner phenomenology beyond guilt-removal. This is the most consistent pattern but also the most spare. The variation is significant:

- **Eze 16:63** (VCG-07): immediate response is shame and silenced contrition — not peace or relief but wordless humility.
- **Isa 6:7** (VCG-04): immediate response is readiness and vocation — the cleared conscience immediately activates responsive service.
- **Luk 18:13** (VCG-05): the immediate posture is contrition and plea-making; the declared response (the man going home justified) implies an immediate relational shift, but no elaborated inner phenomenology is given.
- **Exo 29:33** (VCG-02): the immediate response is ordination-sealing — the atoned-for state enables the priest to function in his role.
- **2Sa 21:3** (VCG-03): the immediate register is guilt-seeking-resolution — the question "what shall I do?" shows the inner person actively reaching toward the atonement act rather than having received it.

The variation reflects the multi-modal nature of the characteristic (see T1.4.1). The only consistent element across all instances is the directional movement: from uncovered/guilt-laden toward covered/cleared — but the inner phenomenology of that transition differs by context, mode, and constitutional level.
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The sustained inner-being effects evidenced in the corpus include:

1. **Ongoing clear standing before God**: Heb 8:12 — sins remembered no more is a permanent inner-being state, not a momentary relief. The sustained effect is freedom from accumulated guilt-burden in the person's relationship with God.

2. **Moral transformation and turning from evil**: Pro 16:6 (M38-D-VCG-04) joins iniquity atoned with "fear of the LORD turns one away from evil" — suggesting that sustained possession of atonement received reorients the will away from sin-generating behavior.

3. **Persistent shame and contrition alongside freedom**: Eze 16:63 (M38-D-VCG-07) uniquely shows that being atoned-for produces an enduring posture of remembered guilt and humility — the person never forgets what they were covered from. This is not unresolved guilt but atonement-shaped humility.

4. **Commission and capacity for service**: Isa 6:7 → Isa 6:8 shows that cleansed conscience enables and sustains prophetic vocation — the sustained effect of lips atoned is lips that can speak for God.

5. **Everlasting righteousness**: Dan 9:24 (M38-D-VCG-07) frames the eschatological atonement as producing "everlasting righteousness" — the ultimate sustained effect is a permanent moral-relational state that no further guilt can disturb.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus evidence supports the following sustained inner-being states and capacities established by this characteristic:

1. **Cleared-conscience relational access**: The person who has received atonement retains standing before God — Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) promises permanent memory-clearing of sin, establishing an unobstructed relational orientation toward God.

2. **Moral reorientation**: Pro 16:6 (VCG-04) and Isa 27:9 (VCG-07) both show that sustained atonement-received state is associated with turning from evil and destruction of idolatry — the inner person's will is reoriented by the experience of being covered.

3. **Vocation and service capacity**: Isa 6:7–8 establishes that lips atoned → sustained prophetic service; the cleared conscience is the permanent condition for effective God-ward speech and action.

4. **Humble contrition as a permanent posture**: Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) uniquely establishes that sustained possession of atonement produces not comfort-born forgetting but ongoing remembered shame alongside freedom — a permanently humbled inner disposition.

5. **Eschatological righteousness**: Dan 9:24 (VCG-07) — the ultimate sustained effect is "everlasting righteousness," a permanent righteous standing before God that transcends the repeated cycles of sin and covering.

6. **Fear of the LORD**: Pro 16:6 pairs atonement with "fear of the LORD" as an associated sustained orientation — the atoned-for person maintains a reverent, God-conscious inner posture.
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, the sustained effect demonstrably differs from the immediate response across the corpus evidence. The difference is in two directions:

**Direction 1 — Deepening and moral integration**: The immediate response in M38-D-VCG-01 is the declared state of "forgiven" — a positional change. The sustained effects evidenced in Pro 16:6 (moral turning), Eze 16:63 (permanent shame-humility), and Dan 9:24 (everlasting righteousness) show that over time the characteristic moves from a received positional state to an integrated moral-dispositional transformation. The immediate forgiveness becomes a sustained moral reorientation and eschatological righteousness. This is qualitative deepening, not mere continuation.

**Direction 2 — From specific guilt-relief to comprehensive standing**: The immediate response addresses a specific sin or guilt-event (Levitical VCG-01 pattern: specific offence → specific covering → specific forgiveness). The sustained effect moves toward comprehensive standing before God — Heb 8:12's "I will remember their sins no more" names not the resolution of one sin but a permanent total clearing. Dan 9:24's eschatological framing names the culmination of all atonement as cosmic everlasting righteousness.

The immediate response is thus event-specific, positional, and relief-from-burden; the sustained effect is comprehensive, dispositional, and constitutive of permanent new standing. They are not contradictory but represent temporal deepening: the immediate relief is the entry point into a transformed inner-being state that becomes more fully integrated and permanently established over time.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The corpus evidences several enabling inner conditions:

1. **Contrition and sin-awareness**: Luk 18:13 (M38-D-VCG-05) presents the tax collector's crushed, sin-aware distance as the paradigmatic inner posture of receiving propitiatory mercy — the person who "will not even lift up his eyes to heaven" is declared justified. Sin-awareness and self-humiliation are enabling conditions.

2. **Faith**: Rom 3:25 (M38-D-VCG-05) specifies that the propitiation is "received through faith" — the inner orientation of trust toward the atoning mechanism is the condition of reception.

3. **Sincere heart-seeking**: 2Ch 30:18 (M38-D-VCG-03) shows Hezekiah interceding for those who sought God sincerely despite ritual impurity — the inner condition of genuine God-seeking enables atonement even where ritual form is incomplete.

4. **Personal identification with the sacrifice**: Lev 1:4 (M38-D-VCG-02) — hand-laying as active identification — suggests that genuine reception involves an inner act of self-presentation to the atoning mechanism, not passive indifference.

5. **Willingness for moral turning**: Pro 16:6 (M38-D-VCG-04) and Isa 27:9 (M38-D-VCG-07) both associate atonement received with the inner condition of turning from evil and idolatry — genuine reception is not separable from the will's reorientation.
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The negative-pole VCG-06 and several other corpus verses identify specific blocking conditions:

1. **Persistent, unrepentant sin**: 1Sa 3:14 (VCG-06) — the iniquity of Eli's house cannot be atoned for because it is persistent and the household has not turned. The inner condition of entrenched, unacknowledged sin closes the atonement-pathway.

2. **Pride and self-sufficiency**: Isa 47:11 (VCG-06) — the proud city finds atonement unavailable. The inner posture of "I have no need" is a blocking condition. Luk 18:13's narrative foil (the Pharisee who lists his own righteousness) implies self-justification as a distorting condition.

3. **Defiance and contempt**: Isa 22:14 (VCG-06) — God's declaration that iniquity will not be atoned for in this lifetime follows the people's self-indulgent defiance in the face of judgment. Willful contempt of the divine warning is a blocking condition.

4. **Hardened indifference to the atoning mechanism**: Num 35:33 (VCG-06) — murder's blood-guilt is not coverable by standard sacrifice because the gravity of the sin exceeds the mechanism's scope. While this is partly a category distinction, it also implies that treating the atoning mechanism as universally available without regard to the nature of the sin distorts reception.

5. **Absence of sincere heart-orientation**: 2Ch 30:18 (VCG-03) implicitly identifies lack of genuine heart-seeking as a blocking condition — sincere seeking enables reception even through ritual imperfection, implying that ritual compliance without sincerity distorts or prevents genuine reception.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — M38-D-VCG-06 names this inner-being state most directly. The person who encounters atonement but does not receive it — whether through blocked pathway, defiance, or permanent judicial closure — remains in the state this characteristic is designed to resolve:

- **Guilt permanent and unresolved**: 1Sa 3:14 — iniquity cannot be atoned for; the inner person carries guilt that no mechanism can reach. The conscience remains condemned rather than cleared.
- **Wrath-facing without relief**: Isa 22:14, Isa 47:11 — the inner person stands before divine judgment with no covering available. The God-ward relational posture is exposed, helpless, judgment-facing.
- **Moral pollution that spreads**: Num 35:33 — blood-guilt not only burdens the individual conscience but pollutes the land; the uncovered inner person's state has communal consequence.
- **Defiant helplessness**: Isa 47:11 describes the proud city as unable to "atone" for the coming disaster by any charm or magical act — the inner state combines pride (still unwilling to seek atonement properly) with helplessness (no mechanism available). This is a particularly acute form of the non-receiving state: the person is both too proud to seek and too helpless to self-rescue.
- **Guilt actively invoked rather than covered**: Jer 18:23 shows that the person who has refused atonement becomes the object of prayers for their guilt's exposure rather than its covering — the non-receiving state can become the target of inverse intercession.

The inner-being state of the non-receiving person is therefore: conscience condemned, wrath retained, guilt accumulated, relational access to God closed — the structural mirror image of conscience-cleansed atonement received.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The primary inner-being dimension is the **moral-relational conscience dimension** — the faculty that registers standing before God in terms of guilt, right-standing, and wrath-status. The characteristic operates precisely at the point where the inner person is aware of guilt (moral) and stands in relation to God (relational), and its primary action is the transformation of that joint moral-relational state from condemned/burdened to cleared/restored. The consistent outcome vocabulary across all VCGs — "forgiven," "guilt removed," "wrath averted," "conscience cleansed," "standing restored" — is conscience-register vocabulary, not primarily emotional, volitional, or cognitive-intellectual vocabulary. Secondary dimensions are evidenced (see T1.8.3), but the primary classification is the moral-relational conscience as the characteristic's constitutional home.
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The primary classification as moral-relational conscience dimension is supported by the following evidence:

- The consistent outcome vocabulary across M38-D-VCG-01 (all 11 verses) uses "forgiven," "guilt removed," "sin covered," "conscience cleansed" — all conscience-register terms, not emotional (peace, joy) or volitional (desire, intention) or cognitive-intellectual (understanding, knowledge) terms.
- Rom 3:25 (VCG-05): "propitiation through his blood… for the forgiveness of sins previously committed" — the inner-being effect named is the clearing of a moral-legal standing, located in the conscience as the faculty of moral-before-God awareness.
- Heb 8:12 (VCG-04): "I will be merciful toward their iniquities, and I will remember their sins no more" — the promise directly addresses the moral-relational memory-register between God and person, i.e., the conscience as the site where sins are held in account.
- Luk 18:13 (VCG-05): the tax collector's inner posture is precisely conscience-register — "be merciful to me, a sinner" names his standing-before-God as the operative reality.
- Isa 6:7 (VCG-04): "your guilt is taken away, and your sin atoned for" — guilt and sin are conscience-faculty terms, and the clearing of both is the primary inner-being event.
- Eze 16:63 (VCG-07): shame at being atoned-for is a conscience-response, not a purely emotional one — it involves moral memory and relational standing.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, secondary dimensions are evidenced, and they do not compete with the primary classification but enrich it:

**Secondary dimension 1 — Emotional-affective**: Eze 16:63 (VCG-07) evidences shame and contrition as inner-being responses to atonement received; Psa 78:38 (VCG-04) involves divine compassion as the source, and the human response implied is relief and gratitude. These are affective states secondary to the primary conscience-clearing. They do not compete because the shame of Eze 16:63 is itself conscience-shaped (moral memory activating affective response), not independent.

**Secondary dimension 2 — Volitional-transformative**: Pro 16:6 (VCG-04) and Isa 27:9 (VCG-07) both show the will reoriented by atonement received — turning from evil, destroying idolatry. This is a volitional secondary dimension. It does not compete with the primary moral-relational conscience classification because the will's reorientation is downstream of the conscience-cleared state, not prior to it.

**Secondary dimension 3 — Relational-covenantal**: Exo 30:16 (VCG-03) — atonement keeps the person "remembered before God," sustaining an active relational covenant-bond. Dan 9:24 (VCG-07) frames atonement within a covenantal-eschatological trajectory. This relational-covenantal dimension is closely adjacent to the primary classification but distinguishable from it — the conscience dimension is about inner moral standing; the relational-covenantal dimension is about ongoing divine-human relationship maintenance.

**Secondary dimension 4 — Vocation/service capacity**: Isa 6:7–8 (VCG-04) shows the cleared conscience enabling prophetic service — a functional-vocational secondary dimension. This does not compete with the primary classification; it is a downstream capacity unlocked by conscience-clearing.

None of these secondary dimensions displace the primary moral-relational conscience classification; they represent the radiation of the characteristic's effects into adjacent inner-being domains.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 silences for Conscience cleansed through atonement received -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The verse evidence is silent on the immediate inner-being response in the following cases: M38-D-VCG-01 (all 11 Levitical atonement-outcome verses — Lev 4:20, 4:26, 4:31, 4:35, 5:6, 5:10, 5:13, 5:16, 5:18, 6:7, 19:22) record only the outcome state ("forgiven," "guilt removed") without any description of the offerer's inner phenomenological response at the moment of receiving atonement. Exo 30:15–16 (VCG-03) records the mechanism and the ongoing relational effect (remembered before God) without inner-being response description. Num 31:50 (VCG-03) records the voluntary offering-act without inner-being response to the atonement received. Rom 3:25 (VCG-05) states the propitiation and the condition of faith but does not describe the immediate inner-being phenomenology of receiving it. 1Jo 2:2 and 1Jo 4:10 (VCG-05, VCG-04) describe the provision and its scope without inner-being response vocabulary. Heb 2:17 (VCG-05) and Heb 8:12 (VCG-04) describe the mechanism and outcome but not the immediate inner response. The majority of the corpus is phenomenologically sparse on immediate response — only Eze 16:63, Isa 6:7–8, and Luk 18:13 (noted in T1.5.1 above) provide any articulated immediate inner-being response material.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->


**Key verses for Conscience cleansed through atonement received:**

**Lev 4:20** (H3722B ka.phar) [M38-D-VCG-01]
> Lev 4:20 Thus shall he do with the bull . As he did with the bull of the sin offering , so shall he do with this. And the priest shall make atonement for them , and they shall be forgiven .
_Meaning of the term here:_ Priestly atonement through the sin offering results in the definitive inner-being outcome of forgiveness — guilt is objectively removed and the conscience cleared before God by the sacrificial mechanism.

**Lev 17:11** (H3722B ka.phar) [M38-D-VCG-02]
> Lev 17:11 For the life of the flesh is in the blood , and I have given it for you on the altar to make atonement for your souls , for it is the blood that makes atonement by the life .
_Meaning of the term here:_ Blood on the altar makes atonement because life is in the blood — God himself gives it as the atonement mechanism for human souls, revealing that the inner-being covering of the soul requires the substitution of life for life.

**Exo 30:15** (H3722B ka.phar) [M38-D-VCG-03]
> Exo 30:15 The rich shall not give more , and the poor shall not give less , than the half shekel , when you give the Lord’s offering to make atonement for your lives .
_Meaning of the term here:_ Equal ransom payment for every life — rich and poor alike — makes atonement before the LORD, signaling that every soul carries equal standing before God and requires the same covering regardless of status.

**1Jo 4:10** (G2434 hilasmos) [M38-D-VCG-04]
> 1Jo 4:10 In this is love , not that we have loved God but that he loved us and sent his Son to be the propitiation for our sins .
_Meaning of the term here:_ God's prior love, not human initiative, is the source of propitiation; he sent his Son as the sin-covering sacrifice, so the inner-being receives atonement as pure gift from divine love.

**Rom 3:25** (G2435 hilastērios) [M38-D-VCG-05]
> Rom 3:25 whom God put forward as a propitiation by his blood , to be received by faith . This was to show God’s righteousness , because in his divine forbearance he had passed over former sins .
_Meaning of the term here:_ Christ is set forth by God as the propitiation through his blood, received by faith — the inner-being effect is that wrath is averted and former sins are passed over, establishing the foundational mechanism of atonement.

**1Sa 3:14** (H3722B ka.phar) [M38-D-VCG-06]
> 1Sa 3:14 Therefore I swear to the house of Eli that the iniquity of Eli’s house shall not be atoned for by sacrifice or offering forever .”
_Meaning of the term here:_ God pronounces that the iniquity of the priestly house cannot be atoned for by sacrifice or offering ever — the inner-being weight is the finality of unatoned guilt when persistent sin has closed off the atonement-pathway.

**Eze 16:63** (H3722B ka.phar) [M38-D-VCG-07]
> Eze 16:63 that you may remember and be confounded , and never open your mouth again because of your shame , when I atone for you for all that you have done , declares the Lord God .”
_Meaning of the term here:_ God's act of atonement for all the people's past sins produces deep shame and silenced contrition in them — inner-being response to being atoned-for is humbled, wordless gratitude mixed with remembered guilt.


### 5.5 Priestly mediation machinery of atonement

     CITE (must quote verbatim, minimum 2): Lev 16:6; Lev 16:33; Lev 14:18; 1Ch 6:49

     AVOID: all jargon from the shared instruction's avoid-list
